The AWS SDK should handle refreshing these automatically. Looking at the current ECR implementation:\n\n```go\nfunc (r *ECR) Credential(ctx context.Context, hostport string) (auth.Credential, error) {\n    cfg, err := config.LoadDefaultConfig(context.Background())    // BUG: should use ctx, not context.Background()\n    if err != nil {\n        return auth.EmptyCredential, err\n    }\n    r.client = ecr.NewFromConfig(cfg)    // This creates a new client every time (not thread-safe)\n    return r.fetchCredential(ctx)\n}\n```\n\nThe key issue is that every time `Credential` is called, it's creating a new ECR client. This is actually good for token refresh because it means the client gets the latest credentials from AWS. However:1. Using `context.Background()` instead of `ctx` is a bug\n2. Looking at the `Credential` method more carefully:\n\n```go\nfunc (r *ECR) Credential(ctx context.Context, hostport string) (auth.Credential, error) {\n    cfg, err := config.LoadDefaultConfig(context.Background())\n    if err != nil {\n        return auth.EmptyCredential, err\n    }\n    r.client = ecr.NewFromConfig(cfg)\n    return r.fetchCredential(ctx)\n}\n```\n\nThe problem is that `LoadDefaultConfig` is being called with `context.Background()` instead of the provided `ctx`. This means if the caller passes a context with a timeout or deadline, it gets ignored during credential loading. Additionally, the config is reloaded on every call, which could be inefficient and might not properly leverage AWS SDK's credential caching mechanisms. The real issue is likely that the context timeout isn't being respected when loading the configuration, causing credential refresh operations to fail silently or hang. AWS credentials chain and refresh automatically. The fix likely involves using the passed context instead of `context.Background()`, ensuring thread-safe access to the ECR client, and potentially handling cache invalidation for expired credentials.
